  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer12059640756051728303">Ramses the Great has reawakened in opulent Edwardian London. Having drunk the elixir of life, he is now Ramses the Damned, doomed forever to wander the earth, desperate to quell hungers that can never be satisfied.   <span id="freeText12059640756051728303" style="display:none">Ramses the Great has reawakened in opulent Edwardian London. Having drunk the elixir of life, he is now Ramses the Damned, doomed forever to wander the earth, desperate to quell hungers that can never be satisfied. He becomes the close companion of a voluptuous heiress, Julie Stratford, but his cursed past again propels him toward disaster. He is tormented by searing memories of his last reawakening, at the behest of Cleopatra, his beloved queen of Egypt. And his intense longing for her, undiminished over the centuries, will force him to commit an act that will place everyone around him in the gravest danger.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_478795746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478795746" />
    <a title="Henry Avila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5431458-henry-avila"><img alt="Henry Avila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307597403p2/5431458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478795746?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henry Avila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henry Avila" href="/user/show/5431458-henry-avila">Henry Avila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345369949" href="/book/show/159501.The_Mummy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478795746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4870826754888344653">Now a novel which includes Cleopatra (VII) and Ramses II, the greatest pharaoh in history has a certain amount of intrinsic interest, especially the Egyptian queen ( with little native blood, almost all Greek) when she plays one of the evil ones. Not a beauty as portrayed in films but attractive, intelligent and a bold capable ruler....Multimillionaire Lawrence Stratford in 1914, unearths his most important discovery the mummy of Ramses south of the capital; however this cannot be since he is in</span>
  <span id="freeText4870826754888344653" style="display:none">Now a novel which includes Cleopatra (VII) and Ramses II, the greatest pharaoh in history has a certain amount of intrinsic interest, especially the Egyptian queen ( with little native blood, almost all Greek) when she plays one of the evil ones. Not a beauty as portrayed in films but attractive, intelligent and a bold capable ruler....Multimillionaire Lawrence Stratford in 1914, unearths his most important discovery the mummy of Ramses south of the capital; however this cannot be since he is in the Egyptian Museum in Cairo, the mystery slowly unravels like our supposedly dead friend's wrappings. Any person who has seen a film about these poor creatures knows the chilling scene: Strange noises heard, the grotesque thing starts to vibrate, eyes staring coldly then it moves inch by inch until the helpless humans, still breathing notice and runs for their lives. Some people's relatives are greedy and will commit any crime to get money, such is unstable Henry Stratford the dissolute nephew of this gentleman, gambling away a fortune, drinking anything in reach and fast women not very quick, yet he is nevertheless his brother's son... A preposterous narrative unfolds how Ramses was given an elixir by a foreign witch that grants him immortality; pretends to die at the age of 90 after a reign of 66 years, roams the world gets bored and has himself buried alive back in Egypt. What dreams he has....centuries of vague pictures viewed and unending, horrific unexplained things, deformed nebulous events..Awakening a thousand years after internment sees Cleopatra's glorious face, then soon Mark Antony arrives in Alexandria. Back to the mummy's sarcophagus and modern times quick automobiles, flying airplanes, telephones which speak until they become rather tiresome to the listener, <br /> monstrous trains loud guns weird clothes and odd customs. Add a few murders, stir some intrigues and a complicated plot a little spice for seasoning passionate love making, Mr. Stratford's pretty daughter Julie has a lot of admirers no surprise she becomes smitten by Ramses the Great and the tale becomes clearer...but the sequel follows so leave a dangling conclusion. This book has many good qualities, yet not enough for it rise above the ordinary just another action adventure story one of countless , if it only stayed on the narrow path and not become unfocused, less is more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4870826754888344653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_482570937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482570937" />
    <a title="Madeline Knight-Dixon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5518809-madeline-knight-dixon"><img alt="Madeline Knight-Dixon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308587835p2/5518809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/482570937?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline Knight-Dixon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline Knight-Dixon" href="/user/show/5518809-madeline-knight-dixon">Madeline Knight-Dixon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482570937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3450688343847967566">I give you the book the movie The Mummy was SUPPOSED to be based off of. In the end they butchered the story so much Anne Rice wouldn’t put her name on it. Which is a shame, because this book is (if not better) sexier than the movie.<br/><br/>A lot of reviews call it “vintage Anne Rice” and I couldn’t agree more. It gets back to the feel of Interview with the Vampire; darkly sexual with the most compelling plot. She’s seriously one of the best storytellers of all time.<br/><br/>A mummy rises, he falls in love, and </span>
  <span id="freeText3450688343847967566" style="display:none">I give you the book the movie The Mummy was SUPPOSED to be based off of. In the end they butchered the story so much Anne Rice wouldn’t put her name on it. Which is a shame, because this book is (if not better) sexier than the movie.<br /><br />A lot of reviews call it “vintage Anne Rice” and I couldn’t agree more. It gets back to the feel of Interview with the Vampire; darkly sexual with the most compelling plot. She’s seriously one of the best storytellers of all time.<br /><br />A mummy rises, he falls in love, and they journey to Egypt where he misuses his immortal elixer. Seems like it would be cheesy or at least silly. But nothing about this is like that-everything about this book makes sense. The way he rises, the way he acts, how long he’s lived, he’s relationship with Cleopatra, how he learns to operate the modern world. Every aspect of the story has a logical explanation laid out clearly within the story. (In my opinion there’s nothing worse than an author having to explain themselves after the book is published *coughStephenieMeyercough*)<br /><br />Just like all of Rice’s other works, Ramses is devastatingly perfect. The woman he falls in love with is fierce and intelligent without being cliche. There’s an older man that for some reason you are attracted to, despite his age. An adorable innocent young man for you to obsess over, and the quintessential bad boy that you can’t help but love. Add in a dangerous and alluring female villain and you’ve got one of the sexiest cast of characters I’ve ever read.<br /><br />The book is fairly long, but Rice is always a fast read. I’ve always found Anne Rice to be the perfect alternative to a “fluff” book because even though there’s elements of a romance novel, the plot is still the most important part of the story. It’s fast-paced and oh so fun.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3450688343847967566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1343303276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1343303276" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598976963p2/6753400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1343303276?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/6448392-the-mummy-or-ramses-the-damned">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=stole-it-from-mom">stole-it-from-mom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=junk-food-reading">junk-food-reading</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1343303276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11393220875940247413">I read a lot of Anne Rice in my late teens. I think I was hoping for another Lestat (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1343302639?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1'>https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>) somewhere in her cannon, but alas, there is only one! “The Mummy” interested me because it reminded me of those super-cheesy B-horror movies à la Hammer, but with sex (I was 17, cut me some slack!). Flipping through it now, I can’t help but think of how my tastes and standards for books has changed over the last fifteen year…<br/><br/>The plot is classic creature horror: the mummy</span>
  <span id="freeText11393220875940247413" style="display:none">I read a lot of Anne Rice in my late teens. I think I was hoping for another Lestat (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1343302639?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>) somewhere in her cannon, but alas, there is only one! “The Mummy” interested me because it reminded me of those super-cheesy B-horror movies à la Hammer, but with sex (I was 17, cut me some slack!). Flipping through it now, I can’t help but think of how my tastes and standards for books has changed over the last fifteen year…<br /><br />The plot is classic creature horror: the mummy of Ramses II is brought back to England, where it is accidently brought back to life by virtue of a mysterious elixir of immortality. This elixir makes him eternally young, incredibly strong and… permanently horny! He saves the life of a beautiful, feisty heiress and they fall in love, and decide to go to Egypt together so that he can get some closure on his long and complicated past.<br /><br />Of course Ramses is incredibly handsome and irresistible. Of course he learns English in like 5 minutes. Of course he can’t resist resurrecting Cleopatra when they find her mummified body. Of course that turns into a huge, violent mess with sexy interludes. It’s an Anne Rice novel, for Pete’s sake! But it’s also fun and I do love the kitschy homage to 19th century Egyptomania.<br /><br />Rice apparently wrote a sequel, where Ramses and Cleopatra are reunited, but I don’t intend on reading it: I’m kind of over her emo immortals and bizarre psychosexual relationship dynamics. But “The Mummy” is good and silly Gothic fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11393220875940247413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2211358975?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨Sumi&#39;s Books✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨Sumi&#39;s Books✨" href="/user/show/62203305-sumi-s-books">✨Sumi&#39;s Books✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2211358975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8775154773275555232">Hmmmm...<br/>Ramses the Great (or Ramses the Damned) is discovered in The Valley of the Kings. He has risen from the his immortal sleep to fall in love with Julie. But when people start turning up dead Ramses raises the seductive Cleopatra from her grave.<br/>Um... Ok. So I read this in October as a good monster read. Unfortunately I didn't really get that. I have a few problems with this book.<br/>First off (and foremost I think) this is not a horror book by any means. I hate to compare this book to her other</span>
  <span id="freeText8775154773275555232" style="display:none">Hmmmm...<br />Ramses the Great (or Ramses the Damned) is discovered in The Valley of the Kings. He has risen from the his immortal sleep to fall in love with Julie. But when people start turning up dead Ramses raises the seductive Cleopatra from her grave.<br />Um... Ok. So I read this in October as a good monster read. Unfortunately I didn't really get that. I have a few problems with this book.<br />First off (and foremost I think) this is not a horror book by any means. I hate to compare this book to her others but unfortunately here I must do so. This is more of a paranormal romance which I was not expecting at all. Although I did like the romance between Ramses and Julie, I have to say the sex scenes were completely rushed and having a very wham bam thank you ma'am sort of feel to them. Which is not usual for Anne Rice who definitely knows how to write a good sex scene.<br />The characters don't seem to be fleshed out enough. They just seemed very one-dimensional to me with not a lot of background to them at all. It also made it very difficult for me to connect with the characters or two relate to the main character Julie at all.<br />The main storylines were okay but there are so many little story lines and subplots that are going on that really have no sway on the main storylines and it seems they are almost there just to confuse you, of which they do a very good job in that respect. <br />Everything considered, not her best work at all. Sadness. I am hoping that her wolf series will be better.<br />Can't say I'd really recommend this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8775154773275555232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172670980" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172670980" />
    <a title="Marianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3555710-marianne"><img alt="Marianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568385353p2/3555710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172670980?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianne" href="/user/show/3555710-marianne">Marianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780701135386" href="/book/show/57860.The_Mummy_Or_Rameses_The_Damned">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555710-marianne?shelf=fantasy-horror-sci-fi">fantasy-horror-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172670980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2352300695347862490">Before I rant, a little background: I’ve always enjoyed horror stories, in particular, vampire and mummy stories. As a young teen my favorite author was H.P. Lovecraft, and one of my most favorite horror stories was <i>The Jewel of Seven Stars</i> by Bram Stoker which is a “mummy” story. Starting in 1984 I began reading what came to be known as “The Vampire Chronicles” by Anne Rice. The first book, <i>Interview With the Vampire</i>, was sensuous and atmospheric and rewrote traditional vampire mythology. Intri</span>
  <span id="freeText2352300695347862490" style="display:none">Before I rant, a little background: I’ve always enjoyed horror stories, in particular, vampire and mummy stories. As a young teen my favorite author was H.P. Lovecraft, and one of my most favorite horror stories was <i>The Jewel of Seven Stars</i> by Bram Stoker which is a “mummy” story. Starting in 1984 I began reading what came to be known as “The Vampire Chronicles” by Anne Rice. The first book, <i>Interview With the Vampire</i>, was sensuous and atmospheric and rewrote traditional vampire mythology. Intrigued, I immediately moved to the second book, <i>The Vampire Lestat</i>, which was a natural continuation of the mythology, and then snapped up the third book, <i>Queen of the Damned</i>, as soon as it hit bookstore shelves in 1988. And that brings us to my thoughts about <i>The Mummy</i>. I read <i>The Mummy</i> while waiting for the next installment of the vampire books hoping to find Rice giving mummies the same unique treatment that she’d given to vampires. Nope. <i>The Mummy</i> read more like an outline of a book -- something she probably pitched to her editor and had published quickly to capitalize on the popularity of the vampire books. The premise was compelling but the writing is purely awful. Sentence fragments and other bad grammar, cheesy melodramatic scenes, trite dialog, and a tendency to slip into the style of cheap pornography insulted not only my intelligence but my sensibilities throughout. Yeah, I read the whole thing hoping it would get better as the story unfolded. It didn’t.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2352300695347862490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_348573802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348573802" />
    <a title="Michael Mallory" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4890153-michael-mallory"><img alt="Michael Mallory" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361841420p2/4890153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348573802?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Mallory" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Mallory" href="/user/show/4890153-michael-mallory">Michael Mallory</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348573802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16034217798814544901">First, I'm a middle-aged guy who does not read bodice-rippers as a rule. Perhaps "ever" is a better word. But I happen to love mummy fiction, be it in the form of a movie or a book. That was what prompted me to dive into Anne Rice's "The Mummy," which, prior to "The Da Vinci Code," was the worst book I could not put down. Perhaps anticipating the Brendan Fraser Mummy movies that came along several years later, this Mummy is not a shriveled, bandaged, mute zombie hit man, stumping around and stra</span>
  <span id="freeText16034217798814544901" style="display:none">First, I'm a middle-aged guy who does not read bodice-rippers as a rule. Perhaps "ever" is a better word. But I happen to love mummy fiction, be it in the form of a movie or a book. That was what prompted me to dive into Anne Rice's "The Mummy," which, prior to "The Da Vinci Code," was the worst book I could not put down. Perhaps anticipating the Brendan Fraser Mummy movies that came along several years later, this Mummy is not a shriveled, bandaged, mute zombie hit man, stumping around and strangling anyone that has p.o.'d some guy in a Fez; he's a reconstituted, perfectly modern-looking, very verbose heartthrob who happens to be secretly a few thousand years old. And therein lies the rub, at least for me: what follows is a post-Edwardian romance novel with some of the most excruciating dialogue on record; Leslie Nielsen should have done the audio book. And yet, I kept turning the pages, in spite of myself. So if you, like me, prefer the likes of a prunefaced beswathed nightmare, dragging his foot behind him as he shambles his way to his next victim, then you may be disappointed in this reincarnation, even though the adventure aspect of the story holds interest. If, however, you're sick of dashing Byronic vampires and want to try a dashing Byronic mummy, who melts the heart of a panting, virginal heroine with a penchant for spouting lines that even Judi Dench couldn't sell, then this is the book for you. "Reader, I buried him!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="16034217798814544901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160999459" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160999459" />
    <a title="Michael Sahd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5264319-michael-sahd"><img alt="Michael Sahd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573161964p2/5264319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160999459?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Sahd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Sahd" href="/user/show/5264319-michael-sahd">Michael Sahd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160999459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1424798044214655085">Ramses awakens in 1914 in London, years after his previous awakening. When he reigned over Egypt, he had learned the formula to make an elixir that made him not only immortal, but superhuman as well. He apparently is highly intelligent, as reflected by his ability to learn English in record time. I personally wonder how intelligent he is, because some of the decisions he makes in the story aren't the brightest. However, his poor decision making is what drives the plot.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice' title='Anne Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anne Rice</a> loves her immorta</span>
  <span id="freeText1424798044214655085" style="display:none">Ramses awakens in 1914 in London, years after his previous awakening. When he reigned over Egypt, he had learned the formula to make an elixir that made him not only immortal, but superhuman as well. He apparently is highly intelligent, as reflected by his ability to learn English in record time. I personally wonder how intelligent he is, because some of the decisions he makes in the story aren't the brightest. However, his poor decision making is what drives the plot.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice" title="Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rice</a> loves her immortals. I think perhaps Ramses is my favorite type of immortal featured in her books. Unlike her vampires, Ramses doesn't seem to have any flaws (other than thinking with his little head more than his big one), but seems to enjoy all the benefits of Rice's older vampires. Although I personally would prefer Ramses' immortality, it doesn't really do the book any favors. A good protagonist needs flaws, and poor decision making doesn't really do it for me.<br /><br />All in all, I've always enjoyed Anne Rice, and I think this is a fine read, just not as good as some of her others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1424798044214655085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_938100988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/938100988" />
    <a title="Tinka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27987005-tinka"><img alt="Tinka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390519559p2/27987005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/938100988?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tinka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tinka" href="/user/show/27987005-tinka">Tinka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=read-in-german">read-in-german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=paperback-hardcover">paperback-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=2-stars-kinda-meh">2-stars-kinda-meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938100988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2163527560840498348"><b>
  <i>“When we are weary, we speak lovingly of dreams as if they embodied our true desires”</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Spoilers...duh</b><br/><br/>Right now, I’m letting out a loud groan. That is all I really can do thinking about this book. Well, I could give you a very impressive eye roll as well. Or I pull out some of my hair. <br/><br/>This was actually my first Anne Rice book ever. I always wanted to start with the Vampire Chronicles, because I really like the movie adaptation from Interview with the Vampire (it is one of the few movies I actu</span>
  <span id="freeText2163527560840498348" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“When we are weary, we speak lovingly of dreams as if they embodied our true desires”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Spoilers...duh</b><br /><br />Right now, I’m letting out a loud groan. That is all I really can do thinking about this book. Well, I could give you a very impressive eye roll as well. Or I pull out some of my hair. <br /><br />This was actually my first Anne Rice book ever. I always wanted to start with the Vampire Chronicles, because I really like the movie adaptation from Interview with the Vampire (it is one of the few movies I actually don’t mind Tom Cruise) and because a good friend of mine really enjoys the series. But blame it on the Book Gods up there or something, I started with this one…and it made me question if I actually wanna give her other books a go or not.<br /><br />I got this one for free and even if the ending tricks you into believing it is actually part of a series, it is a standalone book and I actually believed it maybe would be better to start with something that is not part of a giant series. Sometimes my ideas are bad. Also, free books are bad as well (sometimes…).<br /><br /><b>Writing.</b> It is not that I dislike the writing. It is more that sometimes I found it unintentionally funny. This book basically read like a bad, bad daily soap or at least how I would imagine a novelized version of a script from a bad, bad daily soap. Very short sentences that didn’t feel like they belong anywhere, jumps between action and different POV’s so clumsily done that you actually can only raise an eyebrow and dialogues so flat, cheesy and unrealistic that suddenly even the dialogues from The Spice Girls movie makes more sense. <br /><br />I read somewhere that this was originally planned as a movie script, which probably would’ve made more sense. It would at least explain the weird “cuts” between scenes and parts of the dialogue. Also this book is divided into two parts and a lot of it felt just made up as the story goes along, anything but planned really. So, again if that was originally shorter, intended for the big screen and not as a 400 page novel, it would make more sense. Not that I believe it would have been a good movie, it would have been some B or make that C romantic horror trash, but probably more amusing. Still, I prefer watching the movie with Brendan Fraser and the always lovely Rachel Weisz. <br /><br /><b>Story.</b> Like I said before, this book is divided into two parts and therefore mostly into two plots…and a lot of weird subplots.<br /><br />It actually starts very interesting. Hobby archeologist finds tomb of Pharaoh Ramses the 2nd or Ramses the damned, gets murdered by his evil nephew who is after the family’s money, his daughter inherits everything, nephew wants to murder daughter as well, mummy comes to life and saves her. So far, so good. But what actually happens then is basically just summed up with “stuff happens”. <br /><br />There are so many different plots in this book that I got kinda lost. Not because they are too complicated, but because most of them are either dragged out, rushed, not very exciting or seem just to exist to make the book longer. The pacing is way off and so is the sense making. <br /><br />The funny thing to me is that if the second part never happened and the main plot lines were resolved in the first, making the book about 200 hundred pages shorter, it could’ve worked. It still wouldn’t have been a great piece of literature, but at least it would’ve been more than just a messy theme park ride. <br /><br />Sometimes simplicity works much better than complicated (or wannabe complicated) long stories. Why not just focus the story on Ramses adapting to modern London, falling in love with Julie (previously mentioned daughter) and them dealing with Evil Cousin Henry? Why the trip to Egypt, Julie’s lovesick puppy wannabe fiancé, his depressed dad and most of all Zombie Cleopatra (yes, Zombie Cleopatra, I shit you not)? The book would’ve benefited from a tighter, more personal story.<br /><br />Oh, before I forget, let’s talk Genre for a bit. I heard people telling me how wonderful Anne Rice is with writing horror and a living mummy should be the perfect opportunity for that, right? RIGHT? There was no horror in this book. Fine, okay I can live with that. A Mummy story also gives a great opportunity for an adventure. There is no real sense of adventure here. Again fine...how about just using the mysticism of Ancient Egypt? Well…there is some…but not much. This book focuses mostly on romance, which would be fine, if the romance were written well. It is not.<br /><br /><b>Characters.</b> Oh boy, those were something else. Like the story, the characters started out pretty interesting but it went downhill the more I got into the book.<br /><br />Our titular Mummy Ramses, or Mr. Ramsay, is a hunk, to make it short. Yes, the creepy old mummy turned out to be a hot guy, intelligent (I think), over the top romantic and with a libido that can compete with bunnies. Oh yeah and he is immortal. What could’ve been a tragic, mysterious, complex anti-hero in a more serious fish out of water story, turned into the romantic lead of some Ancient Egypt soap opera. He was interesting at first, but his behavior, his know it all attitude, the very schmaltzy dialogue and his constant crying over his tortured love life made him simply annoying. He wasn’t “please bury him alive again – annoying” but he didn’t make me want to root for him either.<br /><br />Julie is the one that really frustrated me. She had so much potential and started out great. Described as being at her most beautiful when looking serious, an independent woman that wants to stay on her own two feet and not get married just because society tell her two – bravo! If only she could’ve stayed that way. As soon as she meets Ramses her character changes into a lovesick idiot, whom cannot walk from one room to another without getting help from her super hot man. She constantly needs saving, is needy beyond help, cries her way through the story and is utterly useless all the time. She started out as somewhat of the main character and turns into the nagging girlfriend that cannot live without Ramses anymore. And oh is she stupid. She barely has human reactions to anything. Like for example, she knows her cousin killed her father and does nothing about it. She doesn’t tell her uncle, she doesn’t call the police and she doesn’t let Ramses just kill him, nope she basically waits around for bad karma to get him or fate or whatever. Point is, she changes so drastically throughout the book that she seems like an entirely different character.<br /><br />The other characters are mostly caricatures of people. Henry is evil, treats women badly, drinks, has a gambling problem and well, he is a murder. He is so bad, he makes Tom Buchanan look like sunshine. Then there is Alex, Julie’s sort of boyfriend who desperately wants to marry her. He is like a lost puppy and seems pathetic for most of the book. His father Elliot is probably the most interesting character of them all and somehow even likeable. He is depressed, has problems with his age, is married to a woman even if he is secretly gay and misses his younger years. He is the only character with a certain depth. Then there is Samir. He is the Renfield to Ramses’ Dracula.<br /><br />Of course when talking about characters, I have to talk about Cleopatra. Now comes the part where another deep sigh follows. The might Egyptian Queen becomes a sex obsessed Zombie with more psychological issues than any of the Kardashian’s combined. Instead of playing her story as a deep tragedy, she is just crazy. That’s it. Oh, how the mighty have fallen.<br /><br /><b>Romance.</b> Remember when Twilight was published and a lot of people were accusing Stephanie Meyer of stealing from here and there and Anne Rice’s Vampire Chronicles were mentioned quite a few times? Yeah, I guess if she read one book by her, it was more likely this one. <br /><br />Just think about it. Girl meets super hot, mysterious undead guy and falls in love at first sight. He loves her as well but fights his feelings for a while to protect her. Hormones rage. Undying eternal love after knowing each other basically for a few seconds. He struggles with the choice to make her immortal or not. Another powerful creature comes after them. She needs to be saved by him almost 24/7. He is her whole life, everything else doesn’t matter anymore. She is his whole life, everything else doesn’t matter anymore. One of them breaks up with the other, because it is for the best. Girl wants to kill herself rather than being without him, in the end everything turns out peachy.<br /><br />You get what I mean, right? Take that and add a little bit more sex (because as well know in the World of most YA fiction sex is evil) and you have the perfect prototype for Edward and Bella.<br /><br />The romance was terrible and the worst part of this book. Sadly, it was also the largest part. <br /><br />Julie changed completely after meeting Ramses and became just all about him. And Ramses could barely make up his mind who he wanted to be with. Julie? Cleopatra? Well, he banged them both (funnily enough Julie never really said anything about that. Did she know? I can’t remember).<br /><br />In the end Julie briefly breaks up with Ramses because she didn’t want to be immortal and realized their relationship wasn’t good for either of them and too much had happened. I was cheering, I wanted to applaud. It was great and unusual. Of course that single moment of awesomeness had to be destroyed in the next chapter. Julie realizes she can’t live without Ramses and wants to kill herself (which makes complete sense to everything she said before…) but Ramses of course saves her, gives her his magic potion of immortality and the live and screw each other forever and ever and ever.<br /><br />How seriously f****d up is that?<br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b> I hope this is just the black sheep when it comes to Anne Rice’s works. <br /><br /><b>Recommendation:</b> Not really, I mean it is worth a few good laughs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2163527560840498348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_8400014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8400014" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/298306-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369413498p2/298306.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8400014?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/298306-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/298306-kate?shelf=awesomeauthors">awesomeauthors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/298306-kate?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/298306-kate?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8400014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10095216730870758184">Can't believe it took me so long to read this one. There are only one or two of Rice's books that I haven't liked, but this one was classic Rice. She captures the historical mood perfectly, the grandeur and romance and mystery, the eroticism that is somehow woven into every scene, without being trite or distracting. Just when I think I know how she's going to resolve things, she goes in a completely different -- yet perfectly fitting and satisfying -- direction. There are a lot of themes in this</span>
  <span id="freeText10095216730870758184" style="display:none">Can't believe it took me so long to read this one. There are only one or two of Rice's books that I haven't liked, but this one was classic Rice. She captures the historical mood perfectly, the grandeur and romance and mystery, the eroticism that is somehow woven into every scene, without being trite or distracting. Just when I think I know how she's going to resolve things, she goes in a completely different -- yet perfectly fitting and satisfying -- direction. There are a lot of themes in this one that echo the vampires, which was neat to see. I'm not sure which came first, though I suspect vampires were her first love. <br /><br />This novel is the story of Ramses, an immortal mummy who is brought back to life unknowingly by the archeologist who discovers his tomb. It then follows him and the humans who know his secret from England to Egypt, and ponders what will become of the remaining immortality elixir. I recommend this one to anyone who loves Rice, or historical fantasy that isn't too "fantasy". </span>
  <a data-text-id="10095216730870758184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_192295087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192295087" />
    <a title="Sheila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5922167-sheila"><img alt="Sheila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432506364p2/5922167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192295087?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheila" href="/user/show/5922167-sheila">Sheila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345369949" href="/book/show/159501.The_Mummy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5922167-sheila?shelf=rice-anne">rice-anne</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192295087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12463270993761360907">A British archeologist in early 1900's Egypt uncovers a mummy's sarcophagus covered with all manner of dire warnings about disturbing the occupant. Undeterred, the mummy is removed; but instead of the mummy claiming vengeance on anyone, someone else murders the archeologist. The mummy is sent back to England to the home of the archeologist's wealthy daughter for display in her home, and the story takes off from there. <br/><br/>I read this book after reading Interview With the Vampire; this is clearly not</span>
  <span id="freeText12463270993761360907" style="display:none">A British archeologist in early 1900's Egypt uncovers a mummy's sarcophagus covered with all manner of dire warnings about disturbing the occupant. Undeterred, the mummy is removed; but instead of the mummy claiming vengeance on anyone, someone else murders the archeologist. The mummy is sent back to England to the home of the archeologist's wealthy daughter for display in her home, and the story takes off from there. <br /><br />I read this book after reading Interview With the Vampire; this is clearly not as a high a caliber book as Interview. I liked the author's treatment of the mummy and the issues with immortality. I also liked the creativity of exploring the problems with feeding an elixir of immortality to food sources such as field crops and cattle and the horrifying results. The emotions related to and problems with immortality for the characters were well explored. What I didn't like was that most of the characters, with the exception of Ramses (The Mummy) and Elliott, Lord Rutherford, were very flat and one-dimensional. Also, the lack of detail about the surroundings the characters were in really bothered me; I had a hard time filling in the blanks and was frequently guessing. I think this was so noticeable to me because I have recently read other novels (in particular, Gone With The Wind) in which I could very literally see what was happening because of the high quality, interesting descriptions. I found this novel very lacking in this regard. Finally, I found that although the beginning of the story held my attention, the rest was really rather slow and was more of a romance novel than horror or historical. I had the distinct impression that this was more of a "sweep me off my feet" fantasy for the author than anything else, and I agree with other reviewers that state that the story seemed more like an outline and that the ending was unfinished. I didn't hate it but I didn't love it either. If you like Anne Rice and fantasy, go ahead and read it. I was just glad I found it at Goodwill.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12463270993761360907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14816655805932269019">I'd found <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43805.Servant_of_the_Bones' title='Servant of the Bones by Anne Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Servant of the Bones</a> in my university library and had enjoyed it greatly, so I thought I'd let <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice' title='Anne Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anne Rice</a> entertain me again with a book about one of my greatest interests, Egypt. She didn't.<br/><br/>Because of the settings and locations--early 1900s London and Egypt--and the characters--a murdered British archeologist and the main character, his Edwardian daughter--I kept thinking (or hoping) I was reading an <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16549.Elizabeth_Peters' title='Elizabeth Peters' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elizabeth Peters</a> novel. But I every time I thought it, I was reminded that it sadly wa</span>
  <span id="freeText14816655805932269019" style="display:none">I'd found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43805.Servant_of_the_Bones" title="Servant of the Bones by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Servant of the Bones</a> in my university library and had enjoyed it greatly, so I thought I'd let <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice" title="Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rice</a> entertain me again with a book about one of my greatest interests, Egypt. She didn't.<br /><br />Because of the settings and locations--early 1900s London and Egypt--and the characters--a murdered British archeologist and the main character, his Edwardian daughter--I kept thinking (or hoping) I was reading an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16549.Elizabeth_Peters" title="Elizabeth Peters" rel="nofollow noopener">Elizabeth Peters</a> novel. But I every time I thought it, I was reminded that it sadly wasn't by the utter <i>badness</i> that was everywhere in this book. There was the badness of the writing, the characterization, the story, and probably other things that I can't even remember anymore. It was basically a romance novel.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84103154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15625043673865369464">I really like how "The Mummy" started out, and I had high hopes for it. Anne Rice is so good with suspense. The characters seemed full and precise, and I thought the plot was intriguing. However, as soon as the characters disembarked (and you'll know what I'm talking about if you read the book), the story falls on its face. The characters don't follow their established personalities, and the story turns into a circus on a merry-go-round. I've read worse, but I really expected better of this book</span>
  <span id="freeText15625043673865369464" style="display:none">I really like how "The Mummy" started out, and I had high hopes for it. Anne Rice is so good with suspense. The characters seemed full and precise, and I thought the plot was intriguing. However, as soon as the characters disembarked (and you'll know what I'm talking about if you read the book), the story falls on its face. The characters don't follow their established personalities, and the story turns into a circus on a merry-go-round. I've read worse, but I really expected better of this book.</span>

<div id="review_2096931492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096931492" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40275186-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494083045p2/40275186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2096931492?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/40275186-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40275186-sarah?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096931492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7888268786942252997">I'll keep this brief because this is older and it's a re-read. In a world where Vampires and Faerie's rule the realm of modern paranormal/urban fantasy <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43782.The_Mummy__Ramses_the_Damned__1_' title='The Mummy (Ramses the Damned #1) by Anne Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mummy</a> is nice change of pace. Rice writes the setting very well. From a hustling and bustling industrial London to the deserts, pyramids, and shady market corners of Cairo, she whisks you away to with wonderfully detailed imagery.<br/><br/>I'm not sure how well Julie holds up as a heroine 20 years later. She's fitting for the time period I think, but c</span>
  <span id="freeText7888268786942252997" style="display:none">I'll keep this brief because this is older and it's a re-read. In a world where Vampires and Faerie's rule the realm of modern paranormal/urban fantasy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43782.The_Mummy__Ramses_the_Damned__1_" title="The Mummy (Ramses the Damned #1) by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mummy</a> is nice change of pace. Rice writes the setting very well. From a hustling and bustling industrial London to the deserts, pyramids, and shady market corners of Cairo, she whisks you away to with wonderfully detailed imagery.<br /><br />I'm not sure how well Julie holds up as a heroine 20 years later. She's fitting for the time period I think, but compared to the heroines I read now, she fell a little flat (there was a lot more crying involved then I remember).<br /><br />Cleopatra was fantastic. I'm not sure if Rice invented the common horror flick cliche of the mummy/zombie/apparition/whatever dragging their legs and clawing their way to you but the scene evokes a very strong sense of classic creepy. Paired with her sociopathic tendency to snap necks just to watch the life drain from her victim's eyes, this book was filled with all kinds of horror nostalgia for me. <br /><br />The book was nearly 400 pages long but they were pages that zipped right by. It was a fun trip down memory lane and I'm excited to jump into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34400370.The_Passion_of_Cleopatra__Ramses_the_Damned___2_" title="The Passion of Cleopatra (Ramses the Damned, #2) by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Passion of Cleopatra</a> and see where it goes next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7888268786942252997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4419899578563977088">At 4.5/5 stars, the Mummy stands out as one of Ms. Rice's best standalone novels, and is even better than some of her Vampire books (the later ones, anyway) The read is entertaining and the characters are fluid. Not everyone might like this book, but the descriptions have the flair Ms. Rice used to have before her novels started to go sour (around Blackwood Farm/Blood Canticle) and I definitely loved reading this book. I would give this book a perfect 5 stars if Ms. Rice had gone through with he</span>
  <span id="freeText4419899578563977088" style="display:none">At 4.5/5 stars, the Mummy stands out as one of Ms. Rice's best standalone novels, and is even better than some of her Vampire books (the later ones, anyway) The read is entertaining and the characters are fluid. Not everyone might like this book, but the descriptions have the flair Ms. Rice used to have before her novels started to go sour (around Blackwood Farm/Blood Canticle) and I definitely loved reading this book. I would give this book a perfect 5 stars if Ms. Rice had gone through with her message at the end of this book and made a sequel.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2101798110128890689">Cheesy and one helluva good time! My first mummy story. I can’t complain too much. Okay, maybe a little. <br/><br/>Ramses, one seriously hunky immortal, not a mummy per se, he just sleeps wrapped up for long periods of time, like a thousand years or so. He adapts remarkably well. He loves to eat and have sex. An interesting character. <br/><br/>Julie. I positively hated this character. Wimpy woman. Man, was she annoying. Love interest to Ramses. Julie’s name could have been Skipper. Why couldn’t Anne Rice have call</span>
  <span id="freeText2101798110128890689" style="display:none">Cheesy and one helluva good time! My first mummy story. I can’t complain too much. Okay, maybe a little. <br /><br />Ramses, one seriously hunky immortal, not a mummy per se, he just sleeps wrapped up for long periods of time, like a thousand years or so. He adapts remarkably well. He loves to eat and have sex. An interesting character. <br /><br />Julie. I positively hated this character. Wimpy woman. Man, was she annoying. Love interest to Ramses. Julie’s name could have been Skipper. Why couldn’t Anne Rice have called her Julia? Too busy with the vamps at the time to give it much thought I suppose. A pity. <br /><br />Elliott, older family friend, an Englishman. I liked Elliott. Silver fox. Making him come off as some crinkly old man was kind of insulting. He’s 55! Grr!<br /><br />And last but not least, the girl that rocked the house, the bitch that takes no prisoners, the beauty that doesn’t have to try to be, the psychopath I grew to love and adore, Cleopatra. <br /><br />She’ll fuck you and break your neck. Make the sweetest love, then break your neck. Break bread with you and break your neck. Dance amongst the stars ... then break your neck. Have tea and crumpets then off with his head! Hahaha. Loved it. <br /><br />One strong, mean ass, I know what I want Queen. Brilliant. <br /><br />It reads like a soap opera. It is a soap opera!<br /><br />As the Mummy Rots and the Queen Rocks</span>

        <a title="Mojca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mojca" href="/user/show/1359426-mojca">Mojca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345369949" href="/book/show/159501.The_Mummy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=paranormal-romance-fantasy">paranormal-romance-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31642269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9049295548937914182">I don't particularly like Ms. Rice's vampire storylines, so I was pleasantly surprised by the theme in this book, so completely removed from the vampiric realm, yet still firmly entrenched in the paranormal genre.<br/><br/>I'm a big fan of mummies (from cartoons, movies, to books) and Ramses the Damned with his soulful blue eyes is no exception. I loved his story, the trials and tribulations he had to go through and I was rooting for him from the beginning...And was so very happy he got his just reward.<br/><br/>A </span>
  <span id="freeText9049295548937914182" style="display:none">I don't particularly like Ms. Rice's vampire storylines, so I was pleasantly surprised by the theme in this book, so completely removed from the vampiric realm, yet still firmly entrenched in the paranormal genre.<br /><br />I'm a big fan of mummies (from cartoons, movies, to books) and Ramses the Damned with his soulful blue eyes is no exception. I loved his story, the trials and tribulations he had to go through and I was rooting for him from the beginning...And was so very happy he got his just reward.<br /><br />A wonderful, gripping, intense, rather poetic, romantic, angsty, dramatic novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9049295548937914182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2321048904" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2321048904" />
    <a title="Ghost of the Library" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58549808-ghost-of-the-library"><img alt="Ghost of the Library" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585622980p2/58549808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2321048904?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ghost of the Library" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ghost of the Library" href="/user/show/58549808-ghost-of-the-library">Ghost of the Library</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58549808-ghost-of-the-library?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58549808-ghost-of-the-library?shelf=love-beyond-death">love-beyond-death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58549808-ghost-of-the-library?shelf=bloody">bloody</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58549808-ghost-of-the-library?shelf=life-and-death">life-and-death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58549808-ghost-of-the-library?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58549808-ghost-of-the-library?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58549808-ghost-of-the-library?shelf=american-literature">american-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58549808-ghost-of-the-library?shelf=feel-good-kind-of-read">feel-good-kind-of-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2321048904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5920007730360612885">hi, i'm a ghost who loves books, enjoys it when they are made into movies and suffers also from the syndrome - "book must be read before movie".<br/>However, sometimes i am surprised to find a movie i liked - or hated - is based/inspired/adapted/butchering a book .....Jo Nesbo's "Snowman" anyone?<br/>Now imagine my surprise when i discovered that hideous, ridiculous waste of money called "Mummy" starring Tom Cruise and Russell Crowe (what the heck man?you needed a new pool??) was actually apparently - in </span>
  <span id="freeText5920007730360612885" style="display:none">hi, i'm a ghost who loves books, enjoys it when they are made into movies and suffers also from the syndrome - "book must be read before movie".<br />However, sometimes i am surprised to find a movie i liked - or hated - is based/inspired/adapted/butchering a book .....Jo Nesbo's "Snowman" anyone?<br />Now imagine my surprise when i discovered that hideous, ridiculous waste of money called "Mummy" starring Tom Cruise and Russell Crowe (what the heck man?you needed a new pool??) was actually apparently - in a parallel dimension no doubt - inspired by this book yours truly just read!<br />Oh my guardian angel of books why did you ever let this perfectly good story get insulted in such a horrible way?????? ...<br /><br />ok ramblings aside, lets get back to the good stuff, because this one is Anne Rice at her best, and wow there's not a vampire in sight!<br /><br />late 19th/early 20th century, Egypt, a tomb dig uncovers a rather unique find that historically speaking makes no sense and yet, once the scrolls inside start being translated turns out to be absolutely irresistible and the percussor for an adventure that would make a heck of a fantastic movie!<br />Ramses the great, the Pharaoh most of us know from history books, documentaries and those magnificent monuments all over Egypt, turns out to be a very very bad boy who, compeled by a fear of death/wish for power/something he smoked? gets more than he expected when a potion makes him immortal and "dooms" to forever wandering the earth.<br />Yep you got it, the Mummy is Ramses who discovered in Egypt is transported to good old London and awakes to save a human life - yep yep cute girl - and then transports himself and us on an adventure that is a very good mix of an Agatha Christie book/horror movie from the 50's and a perfect afternoon read on a rainy day.<br />You have everything here - dashing hero, pretty smart sassy heroine, sidekick, gorgeous locations, compelling story and yes the usual moral conundrum...eternal life yes or no? <br />For those of you asking - what about the villain? oh there's a few in here...or maybe just the one..i'll leave that up to you to decide ;)<br />This isn't a masterpiece of american literature but within the genre - and Anne Rice's work - its perhaps in her top 5 of best novels. <br />For sheer fun factor alone its worth 5 stars and any fan of the Brendan Fraser/Rachel Weisz/Arnold Vooslo combination called "The Mummy/The Mummy Returns" will have a hell of a good time!<br />Now if only i could understand how someone managed to destroy this perfectly good story and make such a movie mess out of it....<br /><br />Happy Readings! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5920007730360612885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QCWqoXbD7QZq062leFP9GmRvaAuZsPX+ioPith24qKx6A8NzzZ0kbs34GcSPpvfFsjCPw1c9e5nR/aQH0PtaNg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pnQlBujig8gURSrz8LYtMaf88KDkZycXWUIaQUIaQwacUkzUU7xKoLNunpIHQyfucaMXaCrqqXACPFzwj1mxnA==')})
  }

I want everybody to cry when Claudia dies, just like they did for Little Nell.&quot;-- Anne RiceFebruary 8, 1995Interview with the Vampire. The Vampire Lestat. The Queen of the Damned. The Talc of the Body Thief Memnoch the Devil. With her bestselling, epic saga, Anne Rice has reinvented the legend and literature of one of fiction\'s most popular and captivating archetypes. Now, Katherine Ramsland, Anne Rice\'s biographer, has completely revised and updated the ultimate reference guide to the world, history, and adventures of these haunting characters, from the unforgettable Lestat to Rice\'s newest chilling creation, Memnoch the Devil.Written with the full cooperation of Anne Rice -- and now with more than 1,200 entries -- The Vampire Companion offers an insightful exploration, appreciation, and interpretation of all the characters and events, names and places, symbols and themes in the five volumes of The Vampire Chronicles, including more than one hundred pages of new entries on Rice\'s latest vampire novel, Memnoch the Devil. Everything that readers might want to explore further is annotated and analyzed in this entertaining and enlightening work: the unforgettable characters of Louis, Lestat, Claudia, Akasha, Armand, and Memnoch; the important points of interest on Lestat\'s fascinating tour through Heaven and Hell; ancient lore; Rice\'s unique contributions to the mythos of vampires; the literary inspirations that echo through the novels; Rice\'s own reflections and revelations about her work and about the movie Interview with the Vampire; and much more.Richly illustrated with new photos, drawings, maps, and a complete time line of events in The Chronicles, The Vampire Companion is as captivating as the phenomenal saga it explores. It is a guidebook that no visitor to the world of Anne Rice should be without.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"9306083409356359483\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return             if ($('bookCover_67933').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_67933').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer29524811738564719">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&query=The+Vampire+Chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice' title='Stan Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span id="freeText29524811738564719" style="display:none">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice" title="Stan Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure" rel="nofollow noopener">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>

But as these ancient rulers defy one another in their quest to understand the powers of the strange elixir, they are haunted by a mysterious presence even older and more powerful than they, a figure drawn forth from the mists of history who possesses spectacular magical potions and tonics eight millennia old.
